{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01AwwMCqHA8tpHM4Vn8DFKCC","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→//! # The Rust Prelude\n     2→//!\n     3→//! Rust comes with a variety of things in its standard library. However, if\n     4→//! you had to manually import every single thing that you used, it would be\n     5→//! very verbose. But importing a lot of things that a program never uses isn't\n     6→//! good either. A balance needs to be struck.\n     7→//!\n     8→//! The *prelude* is the list of things that Rust automatically imports into\n     9→//! every Rust program. It's kept as small as possible, and is focused on\n    10→//! things, particularly traits, which are used in almost every single Rust\n    11→//! program.\n    12→//!\n    13→//! # Other preludes\n    14→//!\n    15→//! Preludes can be seen as a pattern to make using multiple types more\n    16→//! convenient. As such, you'll find other preludes in the standard library,\n    17→//! such as [`std::io::prelude`]. Various libraries in the Rust ecosystem may\n    18→//! also define their own preludes.\n    19→//!\n    20→//! [`std::io::prelude`]: crate::io::prelude\n    21→//!\n    22→//! The difference between 'the prelude' and these other preludes is that they\n    23→//! are not automatically `use`'d, and must be imported manually. This is still\n    24→//! easier than importing all of their constituent components.\n    25→//!\n    26→//! # Prelude contents\n    27→//!\n    28→//! The items included in the prelude depend on the edition of the crate.\n    29→//! The first version of the prelude is used in Rust 2015 and Rust 2018,\n    30→//! and lives in [`std::prelude::v1`].\n    31→//! Rust comes with a variety of things in its standard library. However, if\n//! you had to manually import every single thing that you used, it would be\n//! very verbose. Preludes can be seen as a pattern to make using multiple types more\n//! convenient. As such, you'll find other preludes in the standard library,\n//! such as [`std::io::prelude`]. Various libraries in the Rust ecosystem may\n//! also define their own preludes.\n//!\n//! [`std::io::prelude`]: crate::io::prelude\n//!\n//!       expr_hir_id: HirId,\n   348→        trait_def_id: DefId,\n   349→    ) -> String {\n   350→        self.trait_path(span, expr_hir_id, trait_def_id).unwrap_or_else(|| {\n   351→            let expr_hir_id: HirId, trait_def_id: DefId) -> Option<String> {\n   357→        let applicable_traits = self.tcx.in_scope_traits(expr_hir_id)?;\n   358→        let applicable_trait = applicable_traits.iter().find(|t| t.def_id == trait_def_id)?;\n   359→        if applicable_trait.import_ids.is_empty() {\n   360→            // The trait was declared within the module, we only need to use its name.\n   361→            return None;\n   362→        }\n   363→\n   364→        let import_items: Vec<_> = applicable_trait\n   365→            .import_ids\n   366→            .iter()\n   367→            .map(|&import_id| self.tcx.hir_expect_item(import_id))\n   368→            .collect();\n   369→\n   370→        // Find an identifier with which this trait was imported (note that `_` doesn't count).\n   371→        for item in import_items.iter() {\n   372→            let (_, kind) = item.expect_use();\n   373→            match kind {\n   374→                hir::UseKind::Single(ident) => {\n   375→                    if ident.name != kw::Underscore {\n   376→                        return Some(format!(\"{}\", ident.name));\n   377→                    }\n   378→                }\n   379→                hir::UseKind::Glob => return None, // Glob import, so just use its name.\n   380→                hir::UseKind::ListStem => unreachable!(),\n   381→            }\n   382→        }\n   383→\n   384→        // All that is left is `_`! We need to use the full path. It doesn't matter which one we\n   385→        // pick, so just take the first one.\n   386→        match import_items[0].kind {\n   387→            ItemKind::Use(path, _) => {\n   388→                Some(join_path_idents(path.segments.iter().map(|seg| seg.ident)))\n   389→            }\n   390→            _ => {\n   391→                span_bug!(span, \"unexpected item kind, expected a use: {:?}\", import_items[0].kind);\n   392→            }\n   393→        }\n   394→    }\n   395→\n   396→    /// Creates a string version of the `expr` that includes explicit adjustments.\n   397→    /// // If we know it does not, we don't need to warn.\n        if method_name.name == sym::from_iter {\n            if let Some(trait_def_id) = self.tcx.get_diagnostic_item(sym::FromIterator) {\n format!(\"{}\", key.disambiguated_data.data)\n        })\n    }\n\n    fn trait_path(&self, span: Span, expr_hir_id: HirId, trait_def_id: DefId) -> Option<String> {\n        let applicable_traits = self.tcx.in_scope_traits(expr_hir_id)?;\n        let applicable_trait = applicable_traits.iter().find(|t| t.def_id == trait_def_id)?;\n        if applicable_trait.import_ids.is_empty() {\n            // The trait was declared within the module, we only need to use its name.\n            return None;\n        }\n\n        let import_items: Vec<_> = applicable_trait\n            .import_ids\n            .iter()\n            .map(|&import_id| self.tcx.hir_expect_item(import_id))\n            .collect();\n\n        // Find an identifier with which this trait was imported (note that `_` doesn't count).\n        for item in import_items.iter() {\n            let (_, kind) = item.expect_use();\n            match kind {\n                hir::UseKind::Single(ident) => {\n                    if ident.name != kw::Underscore {\n                        return Some(format!(\"{}\", ident.name));\n                    }\n                }\n                hir::UseKind::Glob => return None, // Glob import, so just use its name.\n                hir::UseKind::ListStem => unreachable!(),\n            }\n        }\n\n        // All that is left is `_`! Some(join_path_idents(path.segments.iter().map(|seg| seg.ident)))\n            }\n            _ => {\n                span_bug!(span, \"unexpected item kind, expected a use: {:?}\", import_items[0].kind);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Creates a string version of the `expr` that includes explicit adjustments.\n    /// Returns the string and also a bool indicating
